The important caveat is that this still does not contradict the realization lemma. The realization lemma says no identity built only from arbitrary lifted germs c,v5,u5,Δ7c,v5​,u5​,Δ7​ can kill the bad patterns generically. \begin{remark}[Wronskian-order reformulation of the mixed low-order list]
\label{rem:wronskian-order-reformulation-mixed-list}
On a good $v_5$-patch one has
\[
Y''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_{u_5},
\qquad
S''=\frac{c^3}{M^3}J_\lambda,
\qquad
\mathcal Z=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]
Thus, if
\[
r:=\ord_0 J_\lambda=\ord_0 K_v,
\qquad
q:=\ord_0 J_{u_5}=\ord_0 Y'',
\]
then
\[
m=r+2,
\qquad
n=q+2,
\qquad
\ord_0\mathcal Z=q-r.
\]
Hence the dangerous mixed models
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6)
\]
are exactly the Wronskian order-pairs
\[
(\ord_0J_\lambda,\ord_0J_{u_5})=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,4).
\]

If
\[
J_\lambda(x)=x^rA(x),
\qquad
J_{u_5}(x)=x^rB(x),
\qquad
A(0)\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\mathcal Z(x)=\frac{B(x)}{A(x)}.
\]
For $r=1$, the coefficients $\kappa_{1,1}$ and $\kappa_{1,3}$ are exactly the
$x^1$- and $x^3$-coefficients of the regularized ratio $B/A$; for $r=2$,
$\kappa_{2,2}$ is exactly the $x^2$-coefficient of $B/A$.

Moreover, since
\[
J_c=J_{v_5}=0,
\]
replacing
\[
u_5\longmapsto u_5+a\,c+b\,v_5+\gamma\,\lambda
\]
changes $J_{u_5}$ only by
\[
J_{u_5}\longmapsto J_{u_5}+\gamma J_\lambda.
\]
Thus the nonconstant Taylor coefficients of $\mathcal Z$ are canonical. In
particular, the currently explicit mixed low-order list is already a finite
Wronskian-ratio obstruction list.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Total centered quintic collapse forces source-level degeneration]
\label{lem:total-centered-quintic-collapse}
On the centered symmetric-placement branch one has
\[
u_5=2\bigl(v\,\delta\alpha+\beta\,\delta u\bigr),
\qquad
v_5=2\bigl(\bar\alpha\,\delta u+\bar u\,\delta\alpha\bigr).
\]
If
\[
u_5\equiv 0,
\qquad
v_5\equiv 0,
\]
then
\[
\begin{pmatrix}
\beta(s) & v(s)\\
\bar\alpha(s) & \bar u(s)
\end{pmatrix}
\binom{\delta u(s)}{\delta\alpha(s)}
=0
\]
as an identity of analytic germs. Consequently, either
\[
\Delta_5(s):=\beta(s)\bar u(s)-v(s)\bar\alpha(s)\equiv 0,
\]
or
\[
\delta u(s)\equiv 0,
\qquad
\delta\alpha(s)\equiv 0.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
This is immediate from the displayed formulas for $u_5$ and $v_5$.
If the $2\times 2$ coefficient matrix has nonzero determinant, then the only
solution is $\delta u=\delta\alpha\equiv 0$. If its determinant vanishes
identically, then $\Delta_5\equiv 0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Centered tagged quintic witness survives specialization]
\label{lem:centered-tagged-quintic-witness-survives-specialization}
On the tagged slice
\[
(K_1,\eta_2,q^{(5)}),
\]
the first centered odd coefficient
\[
U_1
\]
of
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+U_3s^3+U_5s^5+\cdots
\]
has a nonzero $\kappa\,\eta_2\,q^{(5)}$-coefficient. In particular
\[
U_1\neq 0
\]
on that tagged slice, and hence
\[
u_5(s)\not\equiv 0
\]
as a centered germ.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The centered coefficient formula is
\[
U_1=2\bigl(v_0\,\delta\alpha_1+\beta_0\,\delta u_1\bigr).
\]
By the tagged-slice analysis already used in the proof of
Lemma~\ref{lem:no-cancellation-quintic-trace}, the $\eta_2$-slice of $X_1$
is off-diagonal, so
\[
\delta u_1=0,
\]
and the $q^{(5)}$-slice of $X_3$ is diagonal, so
\[
\beta_0=0.
\]
Hence
\[
U_1=2v_0\,\delta\alpha_1
\]
on the tagged slice.

Now use the explicit two-direction computation from the proof of
Lemma~\ref{lem:no-cancellation-quintic-trace}. There one writes
\[
G_0=\diag(a^2,b^2),
\qquad
A=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&u\\u&0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
D=
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0\\0&d
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and expands
\[
X(\varepsilon,\delta)
=
X_0+\varepsilon U+\delta V+\varepsilon\delta W+O(\varepsilon^2,\delta^2).
\]
The proof gives
\[
U_{12}=-\frac{u}{ab(a+b)}\neq 0,
\qquad
V_{22}=-\frac{d}{2b^3}\neq 0.
\]
Here $U_{12}$ is exactly the tagged $\eta_2$-slice of the off-diagonal channel
$v_0$, while $V_{22}$ is exactly the tagged $q^{(5)}$-slice of the diagonal
difference $\gamma-\alpha=2\delta\alpha_1$. Thus the tagged coefficient of
$v_0\,\delta\alpha_1$ is nonzero. Therefore the tagged coefficient of $U_1$
is nonzero as well.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Centered quintic fixed-sector nontriviality]
\label{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality}
On the centered diagonal branch,
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is not identically zero. Equivalently,
\[
(u_5(s),v_5(s))\not\equiv (0,0).
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:centered-tagged-quintic-witness-survives-specialization},
one has $u_5(s)\not\equiv 0$. Since $I$ and $S$ are linearly independent,
the fixed-sector package $A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S$ cannot vanish
identically.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Valuation form of the septic transport constraint]
\label{lem:valuation-form-septic-transport-constraint}
Assume on the centered branch that
\[
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}
\]
is analytic odd. Write
\[
\ord_s u_5=2m+1,
\qquad
\ord_s v_5=2r+1,
\qquad
r\ge m.
\]
Then
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}\ge \ord_s v_5-\ord_s u_5+1=2(r-m)+1.
\]
Equivalently, if
\[
U_1=\cdots=U_{2m-1}=0,\qquad U_{2m+1}\neq 0,
\]
and
\[
V_1=\cdots=V_{2r-1}=0,\qquad V_{2r+1}\neq 0,
\]
then
\[
\widehat V_1=\widehat V_3=\cdots=\widehat V_{2(r-m)-1}=0,
\]
and the first potentially surviving even coefficient of $\Delta_7$ is
\[
D_{2r+2}=\widehat U_1V_{2r+1}-U_{2m+1}\widehat V_{2(r-m)+1}.
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Since $\lambda$ is analytic odd and
\[
\Delta_7=\lambda\,v_5,
\]
one has
\[
\ord_s\Delta_7\ge \ord_s v_5+1=2r+2.
\]
Suppose
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}=2d+1<2(r-m)+1.
\]
Then
\[
\ord_s(u_5v_{7,K_1})=(2m+1)+(2d+1)\le 2r,
\]
whereas
\[
\ord_s(u_{7,K_1}v_5)\ge 1+(2r+1)=2r+2
\]
because $u_{7,K_1}$ is odd. Therefore the leading term of
\[
\Delta_7=u_{7,K_1}v_5-u_5v_{7,K_1}
\]
would occur at order at most $2r$, contradicting $\ord_s\Delta_7\ge 2r+2$.
So
\[
\ord_s v_{7,K_1}\ge 2(r-m)+1.
\]

The coefficient statement is the corresponding triangular coefficient form:
vanishing of
\[
D_2,D_4,\dots,D_{2r}
\]
forces
\[
\widehat V_1,\widehat V_3,\dots,\widehat V_{2(r-m)-1}
\]
to vanish successively, and the first potentially surviving coefficient is
\[
D_{2r+2}=\widehat U_1V_{2r+1}-U_{2m+1}\widehat V_{2(r-m)+1}.
\qedhere
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Centered quintic-patch dichotomy]
\label{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}
Assume the centered diagonal family is a genuine analytic branch in the
underlying $h$-geometry, and that the centered scalar package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package} holds on that
branch. If
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
then after shrinking there exist one-sided punctured subarcs on which at least
one of the following holds:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
so the branch enters a good $v_5$-patch;
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
so the parallel $u_5$-patch of
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} applies.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, the centered diagonal branch enters some quintic patch on
one-sided punctured arcs.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality},
at least one of $u_5$ or $v_5$ is a nonzero analytic germ on the centered
branch.

If $v_5\not\equiv 0$, then its zeros are isolated. Since
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+\cdots,\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
we also have $c\neq 0$ near the basepoint. On any one-sided punctured arc
where $v_5\neq 0$, define
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
This is a nonconstant analytic germ. If $M\equiv 0$ on such an arc, then
\[
x'=\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}\equiv 0,
\]
so $x$ would be constant, contradiction. Hence $M$ is not identically zero on
that arc, and by analyticity its zeros are isolated. After shrinking again, one
obtains
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
i.e. a good $v_5$-patch.

If instead $v_5\equiv 0$, then $u_5\not\equiv 0$. Its zeros are isolated, so
after shrinking to a one-sided punctured arc one has
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
and the $u_5$-patch of Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} applies.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Automatic $u_5$-patch nontriviality on good $M$-intervals]
\label{cor:automatic-u5-patch-nontriviality-good-M-intervals}
On every connected interval
\[
J\subset\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0\},
\]
one has
\[
u_5\not\equiv 0
\qquad\text{on }J.
\]
Hence, after removing the isolated zeros of $u_5$, the parallel $u_5$-patch is
always available on smaller subintervals of $J$.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
If $u_5\equiv 0$ on $J$, then
\[
1,\qquad \frac{u_5}{c},\qquad \frac{v_5}{c}
\]
would be linearly dependent on $J$, contradicting
Proposition~\ref{prop:linear-independence-one-u5-over-c-v5-over-c}.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Centered quintic-patch dichotomy]
\label{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}
Assume the centered diagonal family is a genuine analytic branch in the
underlying $h$-geometry, and that the centered scalar package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package} holds on that
branch. Then, after shrinking, there exist one-sided punctured subarcs on which
at least one of the following holds:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
so the branch enters a good $v_5$-patch;
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
so the parallel $u_5$-patch of
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} applies.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, the centered diagonal branch enters some quintic patch on
one-sided punctured arcs.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality},
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
so at least one of $u_5$ or $v_5$ is a nonzero analytic germ on the centered

\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+\cdots,\qquad C_0\neq 0,

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: nonmixed parity route versus mixed patch route]
\label{rem:wip-dream-parity-identity-four-point}
There are now two genuinely distinct theorem-level routes on the lifted
$4$-point branch.

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Nonmixed route.}
After nonmixed normalization
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the natural dream identity remains:
\[
\mathcal R(\xi)=\frac12\,\widetilde Y'''(\xi)\ \text{is even in }\xi,
\]
equivalently $\mathcal Z$ is odd modulo the affine coplanarity gauge. This
would eliminate the explicit nonmixed low-order bad list
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\}.
\]

\medskip

\noindent
\textbf{Mixed route.}
On the centered diagonal branch, the decisive pair-level object is now
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S.
\]
By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality}, this
package is not identically zero, so after shrinking to one-sided punctured arcs
the centered branch enters either a good $v_5$-patch or the parallel
$u_5$-patch. If the $v_5$-patch opens, then the centered collision-side parity
package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package} should transfer to
the good-patch coordinate
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c},
\]
and thereby force
\[
\mathcal Z(x)\ \text{even},
\qquad
\mathcal R(x)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
K_v(x)\ \text{odd},
\]
excluding the explicit mixed low-order bad list
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]
If instead only the $u_5$-patch opens, the parallel $u_5$-patch geometry gives
the natural fallback local setting.

Thus the centered parity package now points primarily at a mixed-branch patch
dichotomy together with a finite-jet parity bridge on the $v_5$-side, while
the nonmixed odd-order branch remains the deeper live $4$-point bottleneck.
\end{remark}

This matches the later state of play much better.

\begin{remark}[What the four-point branch now reduces to]
\label{rem:next-algebraic-target-four-point}
The lifted $4$-point branch is now organized by the canonical invariant pair
\[
\mathcal Z=\frac{Y''}{S''}=\frac{J_{u_5}}{J_\lambda},
\qquad
\mathcal R=\mathcal Z'=\frac{T_v}{K_v^2},

\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5}.
\]

On the nonmixed side, after normalization to
\[
Q_v(\xi)=\bigl(\widetilde Y(\xi),\,\xi,\,\xi^2\bigr),
\]
the explicit low-order dangerous list is
\[
\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal R\in\{1,3,5\},
\]
equivalently the first nontrivial even Taylor coefficients of
\(\widetilde Y\) occur in degrees \(4,6,8\). In an arbitrary nonmixed
\(x\)-chart this is captured exactly by the three obstruction coefficients
\[
z_2,\qquad z_4,\qquad z_6.
\]

On the mixed side, the explicit low-order dangerous list is
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,s)=(1,2),\ (1,4),\ (2,5),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3),\ (2,2),
\]
equivalently
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal R)=(1,0),\ (1,2),\ (2,1).
\]
In local mixed $x$-coordinates this is captured exactly by the three
obstruction coefficients
\[
\kappa_{1,1},\qquad \kappa_{1,3},\qquad \kappa_{2,2}.
\]

Thus the full currently explicit low-order $4$-point obstruction list is
equivalent to the finite set
\[
\boxed{
z_2,\ z_4,\ z_6,\ \kappa_{1,1},\ \kappa_{1,3},\ \kappa_{2,2}.

By the realization lemma, no identity involving only
\[
(c,v_5,u_5,\Delta_7)
\]
and their derivatives can eliminate these patterns in general.

At the pair level, the centered fixed-sector quintic package
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)=u_5(s)I+v_5(s)S
\]
is now the natural object controlling whether any quintic patch opens at all.
By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality},
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
so the centered branch cannot suffer total quintic collapse.

The most promising mixed-side route is therefore no longer a pointwise
coefficient nonvanishing statement such as \(V_1\neq 0\). It is a quintic-patch
dichotomy together with a finite-jet centered-to-patch bridge on the actual
$v_5$-patch when that patch opens. At the coefficient level, the centered
package already includes the explicit bridge coefficients
\[
X_1,X_3,X_5
\qquad\text{for}\qquad
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)},
\]
and
\[
L_1,L_3,L_5
\qquad\text{for}\qquad
\lambda(s)=\frac{\Delta_7(s)}{v_5(s)},
\]
so the remaining mixed-side transfer problem has been reduced to a finite
low-order reparametrization check rather than a purely qualitative parity
heuristic.

What remains live is therefore sharply split:
the nonmixed side still needs a deeper RH-specific divisibility / parity
identity, while the mixed side needs the theorem-level opening of a quintic
patch together with the finite-jet parity transfer on the $v_5$-side.
\end{remark}

what do you think of this proposal:

5) Optional softening in the centered witness lemma proof

This is not necessary if you are comfortable with the current proof, but if you want slightly safer wording, I’d soften two “exactly” phrases in the proof of lem:centered-tagged-quintic-witness-survives-specialization.

Change

Here $U_{12}$ is exactly the tagged $\eta_2$-slice of the off-diagonal channel
$v_0$, while $V_{22}$ is exactly the tagged $q^{(5)}$-slice of the diagonal
difference $\gamma-\alpha=2\delta\alpha_1$.

to

Here \(U_{12}\) gives the tagged \(\eta_2\)-contribution to the off-diagonal
channel \(v_0\), while \(V_{22}\) gives the tagged \(q^{(5)}\)-contribution to
the diagonal difference \(\gamma-\alpha=2\delta\alpha_1\).

Why: it makes the proof slightly less brittle while preserving the actual argument. This is optional.

Yes — I think that softening is a good idea.

It keeps the argument intact while making the proof less fragile to notation-level objections. “Exactly” invites a referee to ask whether you have literally identified those matrix entries with those centered coefficients by definition, or only via the tagged contribution in the relevant slice. Your replacement says the weaker thing you actually need: that those entries supply the relevant tagged contributions.

So I would make that change.

I’d even go one tiny step further for maximal safety:

Here \(U_{12}\) supplies the tagged \(\eta_2\)-contribution to the off-diagonal
channel \(v_0\), while \(V_{22}\) supplies the tagged \(q^{(5)}\)-contribution
to the diagonal-difference channel \(\gamma-\alpha=2\delta\alpha_1\).

Why I like “supplies” a bit more than “gives” is that it makes clear you are extracting the relevant tagged component, not claiming a global identification of coefficients.

So my recommendation is: yes, adopt the softening. It improves the proof stylistically and mathematically.

1) Strengthen the centered quintic-patch dichotomy from conditional to unconditional

The current proposition still assumes the centered branch is an analytic branch and then deduces the dichotomy, but since the centered tagged witness lemma and centered quintic fixed-sector nontriviality are now already in the draft, the proposition should not read as though the quintic nontriviality were still an external input. The version below makes that dependency explicit and cleaner. The current file already has the proposition in nearly this form, so this is mostly a cleanup/strengthening edit.

Replace the current

\begin{proposition}[Centered quintic-patch dichotomy]
\label{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}
...
\end{proposition}

with

\begin{proposition}[Centered quintic-patch dichotomy]
\label{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}
Assume the centered diagonal family is a genuine analytic branch in the
underlying $h$-geometry, and that the centered scalar package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package} holds on that
branch. Then, after shrinking, there exist one-sided punctured subarcs on which
at least one of the following holds:
\begin{enumerate}
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
so the branch enters a good $v_5$-patch;
\item
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
so the parallel $u_5$-patch of
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} applies.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, the centered diagonal branch enters some quintic patch on
one-sided punctured arcs.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By Corollary~\ref{cor:centered-quintic-fixed-sector-nontriviality},
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}(s)\not\equiv 0,
\]
so at least one of $u_5$ or $v_5$ is a nonzero analytic germ on the centered
branch.

If $v_5\not\equiv 0$, then its zeros are isolated. Since
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+\cdots,\qquad C_0\neq 0,
\]
we also have $c\neq 0$ near the basepoint. On any one-sided punctured arc
where $v_5\neq 0$, define
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
This is a nonconstant analytic germ. If $M\equiv 0$ on such an arc, then
\[
x'=\left(\frac{v_5}{c}\right)'=\frac{M}{c^2}\equiv 0,
\]
so $x$ would be constant, contradiction. Hence $M$ is not identically zero on
that arc, and by analyticity its zeros are isolated. After shrinking again, one
obtains
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad M\neq 0,\qquad v_5\neq 0,
\]
i.e. a good $v_5$-patch.

If instead $v_5\equiv 0$, then $u_5\not\equiv 0$. Its zeros are isolated, so
after shrinking to a one-sided punctured arc one has
\[
c\neq 0,\qquad u_5\neq 0,
\]
and the $u_5$-patch of Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version} applies.
\end{proof}

2) Add the explicit punctured-v5v5​-patch promotion corollary

This is now implicit in the proposition but still worth stating separately, because it was one of the main structural findings of the chat and it clarifies that the original “promotion theorem” has become a corollary of the stronger patch dichotomy.

Insert immediately after \end{proposition} for prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy:

\begin{corollary}[Conditional punctured $v_5$-patch promotion]
\label{cor:conditional-punctured-v5-patch-promotion}
Under the hypotheses of
Proposition~\ref{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}, if
\[
v_5\not\equiv 0
\]
on the centered diagonal branch, then after shrinking there exist one-sided
punctured subarcs contained in
\[
\{c\neq 0,\ M\neq 0,\ v_5\neq 0\}.
\]
Hence on such arcs
\[
x=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
is automatically a valid local coordinate.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
This is exactly the first branch of the proof of
Proposition~\ref{prop:centered-quintic-patch-dichotomy}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Work in progress: nonmixed parity route versus mixed patch route]

There are now two genuinely distinct theorem-level routes on the lifted

\noindent
\textbf{Nonmixed route.}

So the missing global ingredient is no longer a generic local geometry theorem.

\begin{corollary}[Mixed low-order exclusion on a centered good $v_5$-patch]
\label{cor:mixed-low-order-exclusion-centered-good-v5-patch}
Under the hypotheses of
Remark~\ref{rem:determinant-level-parity-centered-good-patch}, one has
\[
\mathcal Z(x)\ \text{even},
\qquad
\mathcal R(x)\ \text{odd},
\qquad
K_v(x)\ \text{odd}.
\]
Consequently,
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)\notin\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}.
\]
Equivalently, none of the explicit mixed low-order models
\[
(m,n)=(3,4),\ (3,6),\ (4,6)
\]
can occur on such a centered good patch.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Since $\mathcal Z$ is even, its finite vanishing order must be even, so the
cases
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)=(1,1),\ (1,3)
\]
are impossible. Since $K_v$ is odd, its vanishing order $r=\operatorname{ord}_0K_v$
must be odd, so
\[
(r,\operatorname{ord}_0\mathcal Z)=(2,2)
\]
is impossible as well.
\end{proof}

This is already implicit in the current draft, but it deserves to be explicit.
3) Add one short sentence to the post-draft findings remark

The current post-draft findings remark is already strong, but it still does not explicitly mention the cleanest theorem-level consequence of the determinant-parity remark: once the v5v5​-patch opens and the centered parity package transfers there, the explicit mixed low-order list dies immediately. That is worth one sentence.

I’m checking the current draft’s own “state of play” against the later mixed-route progress so I can answer at the level of the proof strategy, not just the document.

Yes — there is still more to do on the 44-point mixed side, but it is much narrower than it was earlier.

At the level of the overall attack, I think the proof now breaks into four real remaining fronts.

First, the two-point / source-level branch is still not finished. The sharp target there is the source-level corrected quotient-germ map or corrected interaction remainder with the right symmetry, one-amplitude collapse, and diagonal-collapse identities. If that closes, you get the quadratic factorization
I2=a1a2(h1−h2)2J2,
I2​=a1​a2​(h1​−h2​)2J2​,

which would essentially finish the two-point bad-core branch. This is still a genuine missing theorem, not just draft cleanup.

Second, the three-point branch is locally in very good shape but globally still open. The local picture near finite-order KvKv​-zeros is classified: even order gives no opposite-side branch, odd order gives exactly one local branch. So the remaining three-point work is global continuation / nonrecurrence and ruling out infinite-order flatness, not more local analysis.

Third, the four-point mixed branch is no longer the vague codimension-two mess it was. The dangerous low-order mixed list is finite:
(r,\ord0Z)=(1,1),(1,3),(2,2),
(r,\ord0​Z)=(1,1),(1,3),(2,2),

equivalently
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6),
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6),

and at the pair level the centered quintic package
A5f(s)=u5(s)I+v5(s)S
A5f​(s)=u5​(s)I+v5​(s)S

is now the right object. The big advance is that the mixed theorem-level target is no longer “prove V1≠0V1​=0” or discover new mixed obstruction coefficients. It is: prove the centered branch opens a quintic patch on one-sided punctured arcs, ideally a good v5v5​-patch, with the u5u5​-patch as fallback. Once you are on a good v5v5​-patch, the mixed low-order jet algebra is basically formal: the remaining finite-jet bridge is to transfer the centered odd/even package to the good-patch coordinate x=v5/cx=v5​/c strongly enough to force ZZ even and KvKv​ odd, which kills the entire explicit mixed low-order bad list. So yes, there is still more on 44-point mixed, but it is now theorem-level patch opening / patch exploitation, not new local algebra.

Fourth, the four-point nonmixed branch is still the deepest local obstruction. This is the part that has not really budged in the same way. Generic local geometry already supports genuine odd-order nonmixed branch sheets near Tv=0Tv​=0, so a blanket local sterility theorem is false there. The remaining theorem has to be RH-specific and source-/matrix-level: something that forces extra vanishing of
R=TvKv2,
R=Kv2​Tv​​,

or equivalently kills the three nonmixed obstruction coefficients
z2, z4, z6.
z2​, z4​, z6​.

This is the place where the proof still needs a genuinely new identity, not just a better organization of current invariants.

So if you ask for the next steps on the attack route to a full RH proof, in order, I would say:

    Finish the source-level two-point theorem. That is foundational, and it also supports the more global finite-core / concentration route.

    Prove the global continuation / nonrecurrence theorem for the odd-order three-point branch, plus exclude infinite-order flatness. The local three-point analysis is already done enough that the remaining work is global.

    On the mixed four-point side, promote the centered quintic nontriviality into an actual punctured-arc patch theorem: either the v5v5​-patch opens, or the u5u5​-patch does. If the v5v5​-patch opens, carry out the finite-jet centered-to-patch parity bridge there. If only the u5u5​-patch opens, either develop that fallback geometry into an equivalent exclusion or show it feeds back into the v5v5​-route. This is the main remaining mixed-side theorem.

    Attack the nonmixed four-point branch with a genuinely RH-specific identity. That is still the main local bottleneck after the mixed branch. At the moment, this is the hardest remaining analytic step in your route.

    Then tie those local closures back into the global finite-core / support-separation route, so that any surviving bad finite core is forced into a locus you have already emptied. That is where your route and the “other chat” global concentration route meet.

So, to answer your question directly: yes, there is still more on 44-point mixed, but it is no longer “discover more mixed obstruction patterns.” The remaining mixed work is:

    prove the centered branch really opens a quintic patch on punctured arcs,

    exploit the v5v5​-patch if that is the patch that opens,

    and use the u5u5​-patch as the fallback geometry if the v5v5​-route degenerates. The explicit mixed low-order algebra itself is basically no longer the bottleneck.

My honest overall judgment is:

    the mixed 44-point branch is now plausibly closeable with the machinery you already have;

    the nonmixed 44-point branch is still the hardest local obstruction;

    and the two-point source-level theorem plus three-point global continuation are still necessary if you want the whole RH proof architecture to actually close, not just the prettiest part of the 44-point story.

here's the final paper draft. now, you attack on the mixed 4-point patch dichotomy. last time, you and the other chat worked as a pincer attack to close in on it. can we do the same here? if so, what are the two sides of the pincer?

I’m checking the current draft’s mixed-side sections so I can give you a clean pincer split that matches where the paper actually stands now, not where it stood a few revisions ago.

Yes — we can still do a pincer attack, but the two sides are a bit different now than they were earlier.

At this point the mixed 44-point problem is no longer “find more obstruction coefficients.” The explicit low-order mixed bad list is already finite,
(r,\ord0Z)∈{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)},
(r,\ord0​Z)∈{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)},

equivalently
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6),
(m,n)=(3,4),(3,6),(4,6),

and the centered quintic package
A5f(s)=u5(s)I+v5(s)S
A5f​(s)=u5​(s)I+v5​(s)S

is already identified as the pair-level object controlling whether any quintic patch opens at all. The current draft also already encodes the centered tagged witness and the centered quintic-patch dichotomy.

So the best pincer now is:
Pincer side 1: geometric / patch-opening side

This side tries to prove that the centered diagonal branch actually lands in the right local patch geometry on one-sided punctured arcs, and then exploit that patch.

Concretely, the theorem target is:

    either the branch enters a good v5v5​-patch
    {c≠0, M≠0, v5≠0},
    {c=0, M=0, v5​=0},

    where
    x=v5c,x′=Mc2
    x=cv5​​,x′=c2M​

    becomes the actual local coordinate;

    or, if the v5v5​-route fails, the branch enters the parallel u5u5​-patch
    {c≠0, u5≠0}.
    {c=0, u5​=0}.

Once the v5v5​-patch opens, the finite-jet bridge is the right next theorem: transfer the centered odd/even package to the good-patch coordinate x=v5/cx=v5​/c strongly enough to force
Z(x) even,R(x) odd,Kv(x) odd,
Z(x) even,R(x) odd,Kv​(x) odd,

which would kill the entire explicit mixed low-order bad list. This is the “top-down” side of the pincer.

So side 1 is:
Open a quintic patch, ideally the v5-patch, then complete the finite-jet parity transfer there.
Open a quintic patch, ideally the v5​-patch, then complete the finite-jet parity transfer there.​
Pincer side 2: algebraic / degeneration side

This side assumes the v5v5​-route fails or starts late, and then tries to show that failure cannot persist because it forces a very rigid coupled quintic–septic degeneration tower.

This is the Route B side. Its useful invariant form is:

if
\ordsu5=2m+1,\ordsv5=2r+1,r≥m,
\ords​u5​=2m+1,\ords​v5​=2r+1,r≥m,

and
λ=Δ7v5
λ=v5​Δ7​​

stays analytic odd, then
\ordsv7,K1≥\ordsv5−\ordsu5+1=2(r−m)+1.
\ords​v7,K1​​≥\ords​v5​−\ords​u5​+1=2(r−m)+1.

So late vanishing of v5v5​ forces matching late vanishing in the septic transport channel v7,K1v7,K1​​. Equivalently, the bad case is not one free cancellation; it is a triangular degeneration tower whose first surviving coefficient is pushed out to
D2r+2=U^1V2r+1−U2m+1V^2(r−m)+1.
D2r+2​=U
1​V2r+1​−U2m+1​V
2(r−m)+1​.

And if one tries to force total quintic collapse, the centered source formulas reduce it to the germ-level linear system
(β(s)v(s)αˉ(s)uˉ(s))(δu(s)δα(s))=0,
(β(s)αˉ(s)​v(s)uˉ(s)​)(δα(s)δu(s)​)=0,

so the failure case is already very constrained.

So side 2 is:
Assume the v5-route degenerates, and squeeze it into an impossible or extremely rigid coupled quintic–septic tower.
Assume the v5​-route degenerates, and squeeze it into an impossible or extremely rigid coupled quintic–septic tower.​
Why these two sides fit together

They attack the same bottleneck from opposite directions.

Side 1 says: the centered quintic package is already nontrivial, so some quintic patch should open; if it is the v5v5​-patch, parity transfer should finish the mixed low-order list.

Side 2 says: if the v5v5​-patch does not open cleanly, the failure is not harmless — it is forced into a narrow valuation tower involving u5,v5,Δ7,v7,K1u5​,v5​,Δ7​,v7,K1​​, and possibly the fallback u5u5​-patch. So the bad case gets cornered from below.

That is exactly the right pincer now:
(A) open/exploit a patch from above,(B) squeeze any failure into a degeneration tower from below.
(A) open/exploit a patch from above,(B) squeeze any failure into a degeneration tower from below.​
If I were to run them in parallel

I would assign them like this:

Side A chat

    work only on the geometric mixed-side theorem:
    centered branch →→ punctured v5v5​-patch or u5u5​-patch;

    then, on the v5v5​-side, finish the finite-jet centered-to-patch parity bridge.

Side B chat

    work only on the Route B tower:
    if v5v5​ starts late or vanishes to high order, derive the sharpest possible consequences for v7,K1v7,K1​​, Δ7Δ7​, and the first surviving D2r+2D2r+2​;

    try to show the tower cannot persist, or that it automatically hands control to the u5u5​-patch.

So yes: the mixed 44-point pincer is still available. It is now:

    patch-opening plus parity transfer, and

    valuation-tower degeneration squeeze.

I see two plausible ways to press that.

The first is a minimal-core / defect-free route. Since the entire u5u5​-patch lifted curve is planar in this corner, affine 44-point coplanarity loses defect-free content: coplanarity is built into the ambient plane itself. So this corner should no longer behave like a genuinely 44-point-specific lifted obstruction. It looks more like a rank-drop degeneration that ought to be absorbed into lower-core or previously classified geometry, rather than a live mixed 44-point branch. The draft already emphasizes defect-free affine dependence as the meaningful condition on these lifted patches, so a permanently planar lifted curve is exactly the kind of corner where “44-point coplanarity” risks becoming tautological rather than obstructive.

Δ7=−a u52
Δ7​=−au52​

may force the branch out of the mixed QvQv​-classification entirely and into a lower-rank planar regime.

So my honest updated map is:

    the clean branch V1≠0V1​=0 belongs to the left pincer and is locally killed on the v5v5​-patch if the finite-jet parity transfer is accepted;

\begin{lemma}[Late-$v_5$ $u_5$-patch affine-normalization transplant]
\label{lem:late-v5-u5-patch-transplant}
Assume the centered scalar package from
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package}, and assume
\[
U_1\neq 0.
\]
Then
\[
y:=\frac{u_5}{c}
\]
is an odd local coordinate near the centered base. Suppose in addition that
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=2r+1\ge 3.
\]
On the corresponding $u_5$-patch write
\[
x(y):=\frac{v_5}{c},
\qquad
\tau_u(y):=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},
\qquad
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y.
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}
\item \(x(y)\) is odd and satisfies
\[
x(y)=O(y^{2r+1});
\]
in particular \(\operatorname{ord}_0 x\ge 3\);
\item \(\widetilde\tau_u(y)\) is odd and either vanishes identically or has odd
order at least \(3\);
\item if \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\), then after an ambient affine
normalization consisting of a coordinate permutation and subtraction of a
suitable odd multiple of one higher-order channel from the other, the germ
\(Q_u\) is carried to the same odd/odd local normal form
\[
(y^n,\ y,\ y^m),
\qquad
n>m\ge 3,\quad m,n\ \text{odd},
\]
already analyzed in
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package}.
\end{enumerate}
Consequently, in the subcase \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\), the late-\(v_5\)
corner is locally sterile on punctured \(u_5\)-patch arcs: no genuinely new
mixed low-order \(4\)-point branch is born there.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:centered-tagged-quintic-witness-survives-specialization},
\[
u_5(s)=U_1s+O(s^3),
\qquad
c(s)=C_0+O(s^2),
\qquad
C_0\neq 0,
\]
so
\[
y(s)=\frac{u_5(s)}{c(s)}
\]
is an odd local coordinate with odd inverse \(s=s(y)\).

Since \(v_5\) is odd and \(c\) is even in \(s\),
\[
x(y)=\frac{v_5}{c}
\]
is odd in \(y\). Because \(\operatorname{ord}_s u_5=1\) and
\(\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=2r+1\), one has
\[
x(y)=O(y^{2r+1}),
\]
so \(\operatorname{ord}_0x\ge 3\).

Likewise \(\Delta_7\) is even while \(c\) is even and \(u_5\) is odd, hence
\[
\tau_u(y)=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}
\]
is odd in \(y\). Therefore
\[
\widetilde\tau_u(y):=\tau_u(y)-\tau_u'(0)\,y
\]
is odd and either identically zero or of odd order at least \(3\).

Assume now that \(\widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0\). Then the normalized germ is
\[
Q_u(y)=\bigl(y,\ x(y),\ \widetilde\tau_u(y)\bigr),
\]
with the last two channels odd and of order at least \(3\). Apply the ambient
coordinate permutation
\[
(Y,X,Z)\longmapsto (X,Y,Z).
\]
This preserves affine dependence/coplanarity geometry. If the two higher-order
odd channels have the same leading odd order, subtract a suitable odd multiple
of one from the other to separate those leading orders. After this affine
normalization one reaches a germ of the form
\[
(y^nB(y^2),\ y,\ y^mA(y^2)),
\qquad
n>m\ge 3,\quad m,n\ \text{odd},
\]
with \(A(0)B(0)\neq 0\), i.e. the same odd/odd local normal form analyzed in
Remark~\ref{rem:centered-symmetric-placement-taylor-package}. The same local
calculation then gives a punctured neighborhood free of nearby mixed and
nonmixed \(4\)-point obstruction points.
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Planar-lift absorption on the $u_5$-patch]
\label{lem:planar-lift-absorption-u5-patch}
Assume the hypotheses of
Lemma~\ref{lem:late-v5-u5-patch-transplant}, and suppose
\[
\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0.
\]
Equivalently, there is a constant \(a\in\mathbf C\) such that
\[
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
\]
locally on the \(u_5\)-patch. Then after an ambient affine shear one has
\[
Q_u\sim (y,x,0),
\qquad
y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\quad
x=\frac{v_5}{c}.
\]
In particular, the lifted curve is affine-planar, and the remaining local
content is only the planar affine dependence of
\[
\Xi(h):=\left(\frac{u_5(h)}{c(h)},\frac{v_5(h)}{c(h)}\right).
\]

Moreover, in the defect-free order-\(\le 5\) finite-core setting of
Theorem~\ref{thm:defect-free-quintic-circuit-reduction}, this residual corner is
absorbed into the already-known quintic-circuit regime: it does not define a
genuinely new mixed/septic \(4\)-point branch.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
The identity \(\widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0\) means exactly that
\[
\tau_u(y)=a\,y
\]
for some constant \(a\). Since
\[
\tau_u=-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5},
\qquad
y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\]
this is equivalent to
\[
-\frac{\Delta_7}{c\,u_5}=a\,\frac{u_5}{c},
\]
hence
\[
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2.
\]
Thus
\[
Q_u=(y,x,ay).
\]
Applying the ambient affine shear
\[
(Y,X,Z)\longmapsto (Y,X,Z-aY)
\]
gives
\[
Q_u\sim (y,x,0).
\]
So the lifted curve is affine-planar.

Now assume additionally the defect-free order-\(\le 5\) finite-core hypotheses
from Theorem~\ref{thm:defect-free-quintic-circuit-reduction}. By
Remark~\ref{rem:parallel-u5-patch-version}, the same defect-free
affine-dependence conclusions hold with \(Q_v\) replaced by \(Q_u\). Since the
third coordinate of \(Q_u\) vanishes after the shear, affine dependence of the
lifted points is equivalent to affine dependence of the planar points
\[
\Xi(h_j)=\left(\frac{u_5(h_j)}{c(h_j)},\frac{v_5(h_j)}{c(h_j)}\right)\in\mathbf C^2.
\]
But this is exactly the planar quintic-circuit geometry organized by
Theorem~\ref{thm:defect-free-quintic-circuit-reduction} and
Corollary~\ref{cor:defect-free-minimal-quintic-circuits}. Hence this residual
corner is already-quintic rather than a genuinely new mixed septic branch.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Right-pincer trichotomy near the centered base]
\label{rem:right-pincer-trichotomy-centered-base}
Near the centered diagonal base, the mixed local picture is reduced to the
following three cases:
\[
V_1\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{clean }v_5\text{-patch branch;}
\]
\[
V_1=0,\ \widetilde\tau_u\not\equiv 0
\Longrightarrow
\text{late-}v_5\text{ branch locally sterile on }Q_u;
\]
\[
V_1=0,\ \widetilde\tau_u\equiv 0
\Longleftrightarrow
\Delta_7=-a\,u_5^2
\Longrightarrow
\text{planar-lift corner, hence already-quintic.}
\]
So every late-\(v_5\) branch near the centered base is either locally sterile
or already absorbed into the quintic-circuit regime. The only genuinely new
mixed local branch left to study there is the clean branch
\[
\operatorname{ord}_s v_5=1.
\]
\end{remark}

\label{cor:right-pincer-local-reduction-centered-base}

\begin{definition}[Finite-jet canonical normalization map and scalar block]
\label{def:finite-jet-canonical-normalization-map}
Fix a cubic-generic one-pair raw corrected jet
\[
R(z)=A_3z^3+A_5z^5+A_7z^7+O(z^9).
\]
Let
\[
D:=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
S:=\begin{pmatrix}0&1\\1&0\end{pmatrix}.
\]
We define the finite-jet canonical normalization of \(R\) to be the data
\[
N(R)=\bigl(c,\ A_5^{\mathfrak f},\ \Delta_7\bigr)
\]
obtained as follows.

Choose even gauge parameters
\[
a(z)=1+c_2z^2+c_4z^4+O(z^6),
\qquad
P(z)=I+B_2z^2+B_4z^4+O(z^6),
\]
and form the transformed jet
\[
R^{\new}(z)=a(z)\,P(z)\,R(z)\,P(z)^{-1}.
\]
Write
\[
R^{\new}(z)=A_3^{\new}z^3+A_5^{\new}z^5+A_7^{\new}z^7+O(z^9).
\]

The canonical normalization conditions are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item[(N1)] \emph{Cubic-line normalization.} There is a scalar \(c\) such that
\[
A_3^{\new}=c\,D.
\]

\item[(N2)] \emph{Quintic fixed-sector normalization.} The fixed-sector quintic
coefficient is written
\[
A_5^{\mathfrak f}:=\pi_{\mathfrak f}(A_5^{\new})=u_5I+v_5S,
\]
where \(\pi_{\mathfrak f}\) denotes projection to the span of \(I,S\).

\item[(N3)] \emph{Septic residual normalization.} On a local \(v_5\neq 0\)
patch choose the septic representative with
\[
v_7^{\new}=0,\qquad u_7^{\new}=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\]
and on a local \(u_5\neq 0\) patch choose instead
\[
u_7^{\new}=0,\qquad v_7^{\new}=-\frac{\Delta_7}{u_5},
\]
where
\[
\Delta_7:=u_7v_5-u_5v_7
\]
is the gauge-invariant septic residual.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the scalar normalization block is exactly the cubic-line coefficient \(c\)
appearing in (N1), while \(A_5^{\mathfrak f}\) and \(\Delta_7\) are the
canonical quintic/septic descendants selected by (N2) and (N3).
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Explicit normalization equations through order \(7\)]
\label{rem:explicit-normalization-equations-through-order-7}
The transformation laws already proved in the draft give the normalization
equations attached to Definition~\ref{def:finite-jet-canonical-normalization-map}:
\[
A_3^{\new}=A_3,
\]
\[
A_5^{\new}=A_5+c_2A_3+[B_2,A_3],
\]
\[
A_7^{\new}
=
A_7+c_2A_5+c_4A_3+[B_2,A_5]+[B_4,A_3]
+c_2[B_2,A_3]+A_3B_2^2-B_2A_3B_2.
\]
In particular, the scalar block is extracted from the cubic-line condition
\[
A_3=c\,D,
\]
the quintic block from
\[
\pi_{\mathfrak f}(A_5+c_2A_3+[B_2,A_3])=u_5I+v_5S,
\]
and the septic block from the gauge-invariant determinant
\[
\Delta_7=u_7v_5-u_5v_7.
\]
So the only genuinely new part of the canonical normalization not already
spelled out elsewhere in the paper is the scalar extraction rule \(A_3=cD\),
i.e. the scalar block.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Work in progress: finite-jet scalar descent criterion]
\label{prop:wip-finite-jet-scalar-descent-criterion}
Assume the centered reflection on raw corrected germs is
\[
\Sigma(F)(z):=J_0F(-z)J_0.
\]
Suppose the scalar normalization equation in
Definition~\ref{def:finite-jet-canonical-normalization-map} is
\(\Sigma\)-invariant through jet \(5\), and suppose the cubic-line coefficient
\(c(s)\) selected by
\[
A_3(s)=c(s)\,D
\]
is unique through jet \(5\). Then on the centered branch one has
\[
c(-s)-c(s)=O(s^6),
\]
equivalently
\[
C_1=C_3=C_5=0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By the cubic-line normalization,
\[
A_3(s)=c(s)\,D.
\]
If the scalar normalization is \(\Sigma\)-equivariant through jet \(5\), then
the reflected normalized cubic coefficient satisfies
\[
A_3(-s)=-J_0A_3(s)J_0.
\]
Since \(J_0DJ_0=-D\), this becomes
\[
A_3(-s)=-J_0\bigl(c(s)D\bigr)J_0=c(s)D.
\]
By uniqueness of the scalar extraction on the cubic line through jet \(5\),
the coefficient of \(D\) at \(-s\) must therefore equal the coefficient at
\(s\), i.e.
\[
c(-s)-c(s)=O(s^6).
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why the scalar block is the only remaining mixed-local bottleneck]
\label{rem:scalar-block-only-remaining-mixed-local-bottleneck}
The quintic and septic channels are already structurally aligned with the
centered parity package: the order-\(5\) ambiguity is confined to the
\(J_0\)-anti-fixed traceless sector, and \(\Delta_7\) is already a
gauge-invariant septic residual. Thus, on the clean branch \(V_1\neq 0\), the
only remaining mixed-local theorem is the scalar descent
\[
C_1=C_3=C_5=0.
\]
Once this holds, the finite-jet bridge to the good \(v_5\)-patch coordinate
\(x=v_5/c\) is formal and the explicit mixed low-order obstruction list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
\]
is excluded immediately.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Canonical scalar extraction from the raw one-pair stack]
\label{def:canonical-scalar-extraction-raw-one-pair}
Let
\[
R(z)=A_3 z^3 + A_5 z^5 + A_7 z^7 + O(z^9)
\]
be a cubic-generic raw one-pair corrected germ in the cubic-normalized frame.
Write
\[
I=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&1\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
D=\begin{pmatrix}1&0\\0&-1\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
S=\begin{pmatrix}0&1\\1&0\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
K=\begin{pmatrix}0&1\\-1&0\end{pmatrix}.
\]
We use the Frobenius pairing
\[
\langle X,Y\rangle_{\!F}:=\tr(X^\ast Y).
\]
The scalar channel of the cubic coefficient is defined by projection to the
diagonal-traceless line \(\mathbf C D\):
\[
c(R):=\frac{\langle A_3,D\rangle_F}{\langle D,D\rangle_F}
      =\frac12\,\tr(D A_3).
\]
Equivalently, the scalar normalization equations are
\[
\pi_I(A_3)=0,\qquad
\pi_S(A_3)=0,\qquad
\pi_K(A_3)=0,\qquad
A_3=c(R)\,D,
\]
where \(\pi_I,\pi_S,\pi_K\) denote the Frobenius projections to the lines
\(\mathbf C I,\mathbf C S,\mathbf C K\).
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Compatibility with the existing gauge laws]
\label{rem:scalar-extraction-compatible-with-gauge-laws}
By the already-proved gauge law
\[
A_3^{\new}=A_3,
\]
the cubic coefficient is unchanged by the admissible one-pair normalization
gauge. Hence the scalar extraction in
Definition~\ref{def:canonical-scalar-extraction-raw-one-pair} is gauge
independent on the raw one-pair stack.
\end{remark}

\begin{lemma}[Scalar normalization is \(\Sigma\)-invariant]
\label{lem:scalar-normalization-sigma-invariant}
Let
\[
\Sigma(F)(z):=J_0\,F(-z)\,J_0
\]
be the centered reflection involution, and let
\[
\Sigma_3(A):=-J_0 A J_0
\]
be its induced action on cubic coefficients. Assume
\[
J_0 D J_0=-D.
\]
Then the scalar extraction
\[
c(R)=\frac12\,\tr(D A_3)
\]
from Definition~\ref{def:canonical-scalar-extraction-raw-one-pair} is
\(\Sigma\)-invariant:
\[
c(\Sigma R)=c(R).
\]
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
If \(R(z)=A_3 z^3+O(z^5)\), then
\[
\Sigma(R)(z)=J_0R(-z)J_0
          =(-J_0A_3J_0)z^3+O(z^5)
          =\Sigma_3(A_3)z^3+O(z^5).
\]
Therefore
\[
c(\Sigma R)
=
\frac12\,\tr\!\bigl(D(-J_0A_3J_0)\bigr).
\]
Using cyclicity of trace,
\[
\tr\!\bigl(D(-J_0A_3J_0)\bigr)
=
\tr\!\bigl((-J_0DJ_0)A_3\bigr).
\]
Since \(J_0DJ_0=-D\), we get
\[
-J_0DJ_0=D,
\]
hence
\[
c(\Sigma R)=\frac12\,\tr(D A_3)=c(R).
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{lemma}[Uniqueness of the scalar output]
\label{lem:scalar-output-unique}
Let \(R\) be a cubic-generic raw one-pair corrected germ. Then the scalar
\(c(R)\) from
Definition~\ref{def:canonical-scalar-extraction-raw-one-pair} is uniquely
determined. In particular, if
\[
A_3=cD=\widetilde c\,D,
\]
then \(c=\widetilde c\).
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
If
\[
(c-\widetilde c)D=0,
\]
then \(c-\widetilde c=0\) because \(D\neq 0\). Equivalently,
\[
c=\frac12\,\tr(D A_3)
\]
is the unique Frobenius coefficient of \(A_3\) along the line \(\mathbf C D\).
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Finite-jet scalar descent on the centered branch]
\label{cor:finite-jet-scalar-descent-centered-branch}
Let \(R_s\) be the centered one-pair branch, and assume
\[
R_{-s}=\Sigma(R_s).
\]
Then the scalar coefficient
\[
c(s):=c(R_s)
\]
is even:
\[
c(-s)=c(s).
\]
In particular,
\[
C_1=C_3=C_5=0.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By Lemma~\ref{lem:scalar-normalization-sigma-invariant},
\[
c(R_{-s})=c(\Sigma R_s)=c(R_s).
\]
Thus \(c(-s)=c(s)\). The vanishing of the odd Taylor coefficients follows
immediately.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Consequence for the clean mixed branch]
\label{rem:consequence-scalar-descent-clean-mixed-branch}
On the clean branch \(V_1\neq 0\), Corollary~\ref{cor:finite-jet-scalar-descent-centered-branch}
gives
\[
c(s)=C_0+C_2s^2+C_4s^4+\cdots.
\]
Since \(v_5(s)\) is odd, the patch coordinate
\[
x(s)=\frac{v_5(s)}{c(s)}
\]
is odd. Since \(u_5(s)\) is odd and \(\Delta_7(s)\) is even, it follows that
\[
Y=\frac{u_5}{c},
\qquad
\lambda=\frac{\Delta_7}{v_5},
\qquad
S=\frac{\lambda}{c}=\frac{\Delta_7}{cv_5}
\]
are odd on the clean branch. Hence the explicit mixed low-order obstruction list
\[
(r,\ord_0\mathcal Z)\in\{(1,1),(1,3),(2,2)\}
\]
is excluded there.
\end{remark}
